<p><i><b>MDNA</b></i> is the twelfth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a> by American singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>. It was released on March 23, 2012, by <a href="/wiki/Live_Nation_Entertainment" title="Live Nation Entertainment">Live Nation Entertainment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>. It is also Madonna's first album not to be associated with <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>, the label she was signed to since 1982. As well as Madonna producing the album she worked with a variety of producers such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alle_Benassi" title="Alle Benassi">Alle Benassi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benny_Benassi" title="Benny Benassi">Benny Benassi</a>, Demolition Crew, Free School, Michael Malih, Indiigo, <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Solveig" title="Martin Solveig">Martin Solveig</a>. <i>MDNA</i> lyrically explores themes such as partying, the drug <a href="/wiki/MDMA" title="MDMA">MDMA</a>, love for music, infatuation, heartbreak, revenge and separation.</p>
<p>The album received generally positive reviews from music critics. Upon its release, it debuted at number one in many countries worldwide, becoming her eighth album to top the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart and giving her a record for the most number-one albums by a solo artist in Australia and the United Kingdom. It became the twelfth global best-selling album of 2012 and has sold two million copies worldwide as of 2014. Madonna went on to win three trophies at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2013 Billboard Music Awards">2013 Billboard Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Give_Me_All_Your_Luvin%27" title="Give Me All Your Luvin'">Give Me All Your Luvin'</a>" was released as the album's <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> and became her record-extending 38th top-ten hit on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. "<a href="/wiki/Girl_Gone_Wild" title="Girl Gone Wild">Girl Gone Wild</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Turn_Up_the_Radio_(Madonna_song)" title="Turn Up the Radio (Madonna song)">Turn Up the Radio</a>" were released internationally as its follow-up singles. All three singles have peaked at number one on <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Songs</a> chart. "<a href="/wiki/Masterpiece_(Madonna_song)" title="Masterpiece (Madonna song)">Masterpiece</a>" was also released in the United Kingdom, while "<a href="/wiki/Superstar_(Madonna_song)" title="Superstar (Madonna song)">Superstar</a>" became a <a href="/wiki/Promotional_recording" title="Promotional recording">promotional single</a> in Brazil. Prior to the album's release, Madonna performed at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XLVI halftime show">Super Bowl XLVI halftime show</a> on February 5, 2012. The album was further promoted by <a href="/wiki/The_MDNA_Tour" title="The MDNA Tour">The MDNA Tour</a>, which ended as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_concert_tours" title="List of highest-grossing concert tours">tenth highest-grossing tour of all time</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"It's amazing to be back in music. I like the intimacy of a recording studio and songwriting. I'm using a different part of my brain when I work on music versus when I'm directing a film. There are a billion more people on a film and I don't have that visceral outlet of being able to sing, scream... jump around. It's very different. I love doing both but it was nice to have the simplicity of songwriting after three years of writing a script and directing and editing and talking about my film, to sit down and play my guitar and sing a song. I almost cried."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Madonna talking about her comeback in music after hiatus for directing her film <i><a href="/wiki/W.E." title="W.E.">W.E.</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>In December 2010, Madonna posted a message on her <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> page exclaiming: "Its official! I need to move. I need to sweat. I need to make new music! Music I can dance to. I'm on the lookout for the maddest, sickest, most badass people to collaborate with. I'm just saying [...]."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> She reunited with producer <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a> over a decade after their last collaboration. Madonna said: "With William, I didn't really have a discussion. We've worked on stuff for so many years that we kind of finish each other's sentences. He knows my taste and what I like."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2011, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Solveig" title="Martin Solveig">Martin Solveig</a> was invited to a writing session in London. Originally Madonna had only acquired Solveig for an idea of one song which eventually turned into three: "<a href="/wiki/Give_Me_All_Your_Luvin%27" title="Give Me All Your Luvin'">Give Me All Your Luvin'</a>", "I Don't Give A" and "<a href="/wiki/Turn_Up_the_Radio_(Madonna_song)" title="Turn Up the Radio (Madonna song)">Turn Up the Radio</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsolveig_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbsolveig-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> Solveig felt the stature of Madonna's regular producers would be intimidating and so he chose to avoid "thinking about the legend, and do something that just makes sense".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsolveig_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbsolveig-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna then enlisted several other producers for the project, including Alle Benassi, <a href="/wiki/Benny_Benassi" title="Benny Benassi">Benny Benassi</a>, The Demolition Crew, Michael Malih and Indiigo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pressrelease_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-pressrelease-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> She also collaborated with female singer-rappers <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M.I.A._(artist)" title="M.I.A. (artist)">M.I.A.</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idolatormdna_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-idolatormdna-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna wished to collaborate with "women who [...] have a strong sense of themselves", she found the pair were "fun to be around" and were both self-possessed people, referring to M.I.A. Madonna said "I don't think she's impressed much by stars and celebrities, so we just got down to business. I loved her."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idolatormdna_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-idolatormdna-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On December 15, 2011, Madonna announced that the album will be released in the spring of 2012 and it will be her debut release from her <a href="/wiki/360_deal" title="360 deal">360 deal</a> with <a href="/wiki/Live_Nation_Entertainment" title="Live Nation Entertainment">Live Nation Entertainment</a> which was signed in 2007. Through this contract, Madonna and Live Nation signed a three-album deal with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>, who will market and distribute the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-360deal_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-360deal-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_single_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-first_single-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2011 year-end readers poll by <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>, it was voted as the most anticipated album of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording_and_composition">Recording and composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording and composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="424" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg/170px-Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg/255px-Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg/340px-Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Solveig_Pukkelpop_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Martin_Solveig" title="Martin Solveig">Martin Solveig</a> is one of the main producers of the album.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On July 4, 2011, Madonna's manager <a href="/wiki/Guy_Oseary" title="Guy Oseary">Guy Oseary</a>, announced that Madonna entered the studio to begin the recording sessions for the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Channel_V_Australia" title="Channel V Australia">Channel V Australia</a>, Martin Solveig commented on Madonna's involvement in the production of the album: "She is as involved as you can be in the recording process. This was a very good and big surprise for me! I was assuming that she would spend only an hour or two in the studio per day and come and see where we were and say, "Ok I like this, I don't like that. I'll sing this. Bye!" And absolutely not... I mean we co-produced the track and it’s not just written on the credits "co-produced by Martin Solveig and Madonna", we literally co-produced the tracks. I mean, at some point she wanted to choose the sound of a snare drum or a synth and that kind of stuff. She was really in the session!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> He felt that he and Madonna had time to spend on the record which relieved pressure from the sessions, and he felt the pair enjoyed making music together which was the reason for which they continued past one song which had been the original concept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsolveig_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbsolveig-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Solveig and Madonna "got along very well" and found common interests in music, cinema, food and wine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsolveig_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-bbsolveig-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Common interests in the French film <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Samoura%C3%AF" title="Le Samouraï">Le Samouraï</a></i> about a solitary killer became a discussion which led to Solveig drafting the song "Beautiful Killer" in reference to the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsolveig_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-bbsolveig-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> When discussing Solveig, Madonna found their common interests were what drove them to have successful collaborations, she liked his way of working saying "He’s very organised and methodical in his thinking" and she found she was able to say "‘No, I don’t like that,’ and you’re not going to hurt [his] feelings".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idolatormdna_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-idolatormdna-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna also talked about producer William Orbit, she felt her European qualities were well suited to his production style, and with conversation during sessions being "essential" she felt "With William, we always get into discussions about philosophy or quantum physics".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idolatormdna_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-idolatormdna-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> When it came to working with Benny and Alle Benassi she found it difficult to communicate with Benny as he is not fluent in English, during their recording sessions she used his cousin Allessandro as an interpreter and whilst this originally proved frustrating they eventually found a way to communicate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idolatormdna_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-idolatormdna-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> She had not worked with Benny Benassi before and found that the first-time meeting a producer was difficult as she would feel shy, but after they had solved the communication troubles Madonna found "I felt like I knew him very well".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idolatormdna_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-idolatormdna-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"I'm Addicted" was written and produced by Madonna, Alle Benassi and Benny Benassi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardcredits_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboardcredits-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> It is an <a href="/wiki/Electro_house" title="Electro house">electro house</a> song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-star_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-star-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> with synth sequences build into fizzing swells and stabs, bleeping and swooshing all the way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Star_Observer" title="Star Observer">Star Observer</a>, the track builds from quiet verses into an ear-splitting ’90s house chorus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-star_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-star-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> While Michael Cragg of <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a> wrote the song has "squiggly synth squelches and a beat that morphs into a fairly ridiculous <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Harris" title="Calvin Harris">Calvin Harris</a>-esque breakdown."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Nick Levine of <a href="/wiki/The_National_(Abu_Dhabi)" title="The National (Abu Dhabi)">The National</a>, it is a song that’s like a post-<a href="/wiki/David_Guetta" title="David Guetta">Guetta</a> take on her mid-Noughties work <i><a href="/wiki/Confessions_on_a_Dance_Floor" title="Confessions on a Dance Floor">Confessions on a Dance Floor</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-national_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-national-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Lyrically, it talks about being addicted to love, comparing the rush of hormones with narcotics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titling_and_artwork">Titling and artwork</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Titling and artwork">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The album's title was announced by Madonna during an interview on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Graham_Norton_Show" title="The Graham Norton Show">The Graham Norton Show</a></i> on January 11, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Martin Solveig revealed that it was M.I.A. who suggested the album title to Madonna, noting "We were having a lot of fun with the initials. M.I.A. said, 'You should call your album <i>MDNA</i> because it would be a good <a href="/wiki/Abbreviation" title="Abbreviation">abbreviation</a> and spelling of your name.' Then we realized that there were actually many different possibilities of understanding for those initials—the most important being the <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> of Madonna."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> When discussing the album on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</a></i>, Madonna explained that the album's title is a <a href="/wiki/Double_entendre" title="Double entendre">triple entendre</a>, representing both her name and "Madonna DNA". She also implied that the title is a reference to the drug <a href="/wiki/MDMA" title="MDMA">MDMA</a>, or ecstasy, which provides "euphoric feelings of love".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> It was condemned by Lucy Dawe, a spokesperson for the anti-drugs campaign group <i>Cannabis Skunk Sense</i>. She told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> newspaper that Madonna's choice of album title was "an ill advised decision."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anti-drugs_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-anti-drugs-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album's artwork was shot by <a href="/wiki/Mert_and_Marcus" title="Mert and Marcus">Mert and Marcus</a> and directed by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bianco" title="Giovanni Bianco">Giovanni Bianco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna wore a red dress by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Berardi" title="Antonio Berardi">Antonio Berardi</a>, with futuristic padded shoulders, along with fingerless gloves and red lipstick. <a href="/wiki/Arianne_Phillips" title="Arianne Phillips">Arianne Phillips</a>, who worked with Madonna for her previous tours, styled the singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Jocelyn Vena of <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a>, in the artwork, the singer "cocks her head up, her curly hair pulled back... The photo has some kind of broken mirror filter over it, giving it a funky, dance-queen vibe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvart_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvart-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Vena also commented that Madonna is "truly expressing herself in the glamorous, deconstructed photograph full of bouncing colors."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvart_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvart-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Robbie Daw of <a href="/wiki/Idolator_(website)" title="Idolator (website)">Idolator</a> compared the artwork to the one of <i><a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_album)" title="True Blue (Madonna album)">True Blue</a></i> (1986).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Emily Hewett from <i><a href="/wiki/Metro_(British_newspaper)" title="Metro (British newspaper)">Metro</a></i> wrote that "although the latest cover shares similar colours and the same blurred style with the deluxe edition, the standard version features a close-up body shot of the American singer wearing a tight-fitting scarlet dress and fingerless gloves to match, rather than a head shot."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Dale Eisinger from <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> magazine listed the cover as the eleventh best album artwork of the past five years, explaining: "Vaguely hallucinatory in color and presentation, the cover of [<i>MDNA</i>] is as vibrant as it was bold. Featuring the performer wearing a scarlet dress behind ribbed glass, she looks fragmented, deconstructed by the various lenses she's been put under throughout the years. In this case, it is through the lens of photographers Mert Alas and Marcus Piggott... Though they've done album covers for countless pop stars, Mert and Marcus achieve something truly eye-popping on this cover, even if that was through digital manipulation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Super_Bowl">Super Bowl</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Super Bowl">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XLVI halftime show">Super Bowl XLVI halftime show</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1657" data-file-width="1827" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg/220px-Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg/330px-Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg/440px-Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madonna_Super_Bowl_2012.1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing "Give Me All Your Luvin'" at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In December 2011, it was announced that Madonna would perform at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XLVI halftime show">Super Bowl XLVI halftime show</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Oil_Stadium" title="Lucas Oil Stadium">Lucas Oil Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>. Madonna collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Cirque_du_Soleil" title="Cirque du Soleil">Cirque du Soleil</a> in producing the show, and was chosen in lieu of American recording artist <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Rehearsal for the halftime performance accumulated to an estimated 320 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The show was visualized by Cirque Du Soleil and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_King" title="Jamie King">Jamie King</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nfl12_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-nfl12-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna performed at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XLVI halftime show">Bridgestone Halftime Show</a> which was broadcast on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> on February 5, 2012, from Lucas Oil Stadium. The performance included twenty dancing dolls, seventeen main dancers, a two hundred membered church choir, and a drumline consisting of a hundred percussionists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Thirty-six image projectors were utilized to create a spectacle of lights, while Madonna wore 120 individual prosthetic eyelashes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The show began with Madonna being carried into the stadium by 150 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bearer_(carrier)" title="Bearer (carrier)">bearers</a>, who wore pairs of black underwear designed by <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Klein" title="Calvin Klein">Calvin Klein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> She arrived atop of a golden throne, which weighed over 1,200 pounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> and sported a long golden cape designed by <a href="/wiki/Givenchy" title="Givenchy">Givenchy</a>; completion of the cape happened over an approximate period of 750 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna performed "<a href="/wiki/Give_Me_All_Your_Luvin%27" title="Give Me All Your Luvin'">Give Me All Your Luvin'</a>" (joined by <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M.I.A._(artist)" title="M.I.A. (artist)">M.I.A.</a> dressed as cheerleaders), during a medley of her past hits "<a href="/wiki/Vogue_(Madonna_song)" title="Vogue (Madonna song)">Vogue</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>" (performed with <a href="/wiki/LMFAO" title="LMFAO">LMFAO</a> along with excerpts from "<a href="/wiki/Party_Rock_Anthem" title="Party Rock Anthem">Party Rock Anthem</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Sexy_and_I_Know_It" title="Sexy and I Know It">Sexy and I Know It</a>"), then an "<a href="/wiki/Open_Your_Heart_(Madonna_song)" title="Open Your Heart (Madonna song)">Open Your Heart</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/Express_Yourself_(Madonna_song)" title="Express Yourself (Madonna song)">Express Yourself</a>" interlude followed by "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(song)" title="Like a Prayer (song)">Like a Prayer</a>" (performed with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cee_Lo_Green" title="Cee Lo Green">Cee Lo Green</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Once the show concluded, a group of 250 volunteers dismantled the stage in six minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv2_32-6"><a href="#cite_note-mtv2-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The performance gained widespread attention from the media, after M.I.A. extended the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finger_(gesture)" title="Finger (gesture)">middle finger</a> to the camera near the end of her verse of the song instead of singing the word "shit".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The incident prompted broadcaster <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> to issue apologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's performance broke a record as the most-watched Super Bowl halftime show in history, garnering 114 million viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> She also set a new record as the most <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeted</a> about subject on the social network <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> with 10,245 posts per second and was the most-searched term on <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> during the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna was not paid for the performance, as previous performers at the event have not been paid. However, a <i>Forbes</i> analysis said before the event that, with 30-second commercial spots commanding over $3 million apiece, the 12 minutes of free television exposure had a considerable promotional value to Madonna's multiple enterprises coming to market at the time of the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following her performance at the Super Bowl, the album received limited promotion and Madonna was basically off the radar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_2nd_week_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_2nd_week-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone2_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone2-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> She avoided major television appearances and live performances, instead focusing on rehearsals for her world tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone2_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone2-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> On April 11, 2012, her manager Guy Oseary explained on his Twitter: "I wish we could have done TV last week but we were in rehearsals morning and night."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_2nd_week_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_2nd_week-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna used <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a> to promote the album instead. Through her official Facebook, she published minute-long snippets of several album tracks, posted behind-the-scenes pictures of tour rehearsals and polled her fans about which back-catalog songs they'd like to hear when she hits the road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> On March 24, 2012, Madonna took a livestream chat on Facebook with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Fallon" title="Jimmy Fallon">Jimmy Fallon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> She later made a brief appearance on <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Music_Festival" title="Ultra Music Festival">Ultra Music Festival 14</a> in Miami on March 2012, where she introduced Swedish DJ <a href="/wiki/Avicii" title="Avicii">Avicii</a> and his remix of her single, "Girl Gone Wild".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon the album's sales drop in its second week, critics and fans criticized the lack of promotion and poor singles choices for the album. Through his Facebook, producer William Orbit expressed his displeasure of the album's poor promotion, and said that they had little time to record the album because Madonna's schedule was packed full of other commitments, such as "<a href="/wiki/Truth_or_Dare_by_Madonna" title="Truth or Dare by Madonna">perfume ranges</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_fashion_brands_by_Madonna#Material_Girl" title="List of fashion brands by Madonna">teen fashion contests</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Orbit later apologized for the statement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-promo_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-promo-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tour">Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_MDNA_Tour" title="The MDNA Tour">The MDNA Tour</a></div>
<p>Madonna announced her ninth concert tour on February 7, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour was launched on May 31 in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and ended in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> in December 2012. It marked her biggest tour ever with 88 shows and included many markets she had never played before. This tour played 32 dates in 28 European markets, including <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, before hitting North America with 45 shows. The tour was promoted by <a href="/wiki/Live_Nation_Entertainment" title="Live Nation Entertainment">Live Nation Entertainment</a> as part of a <a href="/wiki/360_deal" title="360 deal">360 deal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> On March 26, Madonna had confirmed the tour title, <a href="/wiki/The_MDNA_Tour" title="The MDNA Tour">The MDNA Tour</a> via <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> It became the highest-grossing tour of 2012 and 10th <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_concert_tours" title="List of highest-grossing concert tours">highest-grossing tour of all time</a>, grossing $305.1 million in ticket sales for 88 sold-out shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Give_Me_All_Your_Luvin%27" title="Give Me All Your Luvin'">Give Me All Your Luvin'</a>" was released as the first single from the album on February 3, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pressrelease_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-pressrelease-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> It received mixed reception from critics, who complimented its "catchy" melodies, but felt that the musical composition is inferior to Madonna's previous singles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Many reviewers noted the song as a weak lead single and not a proper representation of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Petridis_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Petridis-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The song reached the top of the charts in Canada, Finland, Hungary, Israel, and Venezuela, and the top five in several European countries, Japan and South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> It became Madonna's 38th top-ten hit on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, extending her record as the artist with most top-ten singles in the chart history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Its accompanying music video was directed by Megaforce and features football and cheerleader theme inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Girl_Gone_Wild" title="Girl Gone Wild">Girl Gone Wild</a>" was released digitally on March 2, 2012. It also was met with mixed critical reception, with critics praising the dance nature of the song, while some noting its similarities to songs from other mainstream artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> The black-and-white music video for the song was directed by fashion photographers <a href="/wiki/Mert_and_Marcus" title="Mert and Marcus">Mert and Marcus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Masterpiece_(Madonna_song)" title="Masterpiece (Madonna song)">Masterpiece</a>" was officially sent to radio stations in the United Kingdom on April 2, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radio_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-radio-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The song also reached the top of the Russian Top 100 Airplay chart on December 2, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> In Brazil, "<a href="/wiki/Superstar_(Madonna_song)" title="Superstar (Madonna song)">Superstar</a>" was released on December 3, 2012 only as a special edition free CD with Brazilian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Folha_de_S._Paulo" title="Folha de S. Paulo">Folha de S. Paulo</a></i>. The accompanying artwork for the single was created by Brazilian graffitist Simone Sapienza who won a contest sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Johnnie_Walker" title="Johnnie Walker">Johnnie Walker</a>'s Keep Walking Project in Brazil, she was chosen by Madonna after being among ten finalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Turn_Up_the_Radio_(Madonna_song)" title="Turn Up the Radio (Madonna song)">Turn Up the Radio</a>" was released as the final single from the album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> on August 5, 2012 in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="vertical-align:middle">7/10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ganz_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ganz-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></td>

<p><i>MDNA</i> received generally positive reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_criticism" title="Music criticism">music critics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream critics, the album received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">average</a> score of 64, based on 34 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MC_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-MC-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> wrote that it "represents a determined, no-nonsense restatement of the Madonna brand following the lacklustre <i>Hard Candy</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gill_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gill-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> writer Joe Levy called the album a "disco-fied divorce record" and wrote of its music, "there's lots of naughtiness for the DJ to bring back, and the music has depth that rewards repeated listening."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levy_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Levy-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Priya Elan of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> called <i>MDNA</i> "a ridiculously enjoyable romp", citing its "psychotic, soul-bearing stuff" as "some of the most visceral stuff she’s ever done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elan_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elan-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>'s Sal Cinquemani found the album "surprisingly cohesive despite its seven-plus producers" and stated, "it's obvious <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madge</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">Billy Bubbles</a> can still create magic together."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cinquemani_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cinquemani-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Enio Chiola of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> wrote that she "deftly juggles the production variances" and called it "a welcome return to form in so many different ways."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chiola_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chiola-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kot" title="Greg Kot">Greg Kot</a> called it her best album since <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i> (1998) and wrote that she "excels" on the William Orbit-produced tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kot_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kot-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Caryn Ganz of <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> commented similarly, "if there's one producer who knows how to pluck Madonna's heartstrings, it's <i>Ray of Light</i> '​s Orbit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ganz_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ganz-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jon_Pareles" title="Jon Pareles">Jon Pareles</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> viewed that Madonna's "pop instinct, the one that hones catchiness above all [...] gets her through <i>MDNA</i> with hook after hook."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pareles_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pareles-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> found the album "flinty" and "excessively lean" as a result of "cool calculations" aimed to reassert Madonna's preeminence in dance and pop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Erlewine_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Erlewine-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Helen Brown of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> panned its lyrics as "horribly cliched" and criticized Madonna's direction, stating "a woman who’s putting so much visibly desperate energy into looking and sounding like a teenager is missing the point of pop, of parties ... of life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a>'s Matthew Perpetua found most of it "shockingly banal" and "particularly hollow, the dead-eyed result of obligations, deadlines, and hedged bets."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perpetua_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Perpetua-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maura_Johnston" title="Maura Johnston">Maura Johnston</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> found Madonna's "move toward <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">EDM</a> [...] hamfisted" and found her voice to be a "nonpresence".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnston_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writer Randall Roberts viewed that its music suffers from "familiarity" and that the album "offers evidence that the singer has fallen behind, that she is no longer setting the conversation" in pop music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Genevieve Koski of <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> criticized its "electronically manipulated" vocals and "big, generic Euro-dance beats", while calling <i>MDNA</i> "competent, but equally perfunctory."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koski_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Koski-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Petridis" title="Alexis Petridis">Alexis Petridis</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> viewed the album as "neither triumph nor disaster", writing that it "turns out to be just another Madonna album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Petridis_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-Petridis-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with 359,000 copies sold in the United States, making it her biggest opening week sales since <i><a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_album)" title="Music (Madonna album)">Music</a></i> (2000). It became Madonna's eighth chart-topper and her fifth consecutive studio album to debut at number one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bb200_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-bb200-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's sales were aided by Madonna's tour audience, who had an option to get the album as part of their ticket purchase. Around 185,000 copies of first week sales reportedly came from that album-ticket bundling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> In its second week, the album descended to number eight with 48,000 copies or about 86.7% sales decrease, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way" title="Born This Way">Born This Way</a></i> (2011) for the biggest second-week percentage drop for a number-one debuting album in the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_2nd_week_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_2nd_week-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 9, 2012, <i>MDNA</i> was certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) for shipment of 500,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaa-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2014, it has sold 537,000 copies in the United States, according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_sales_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_sales-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> In Canada, <i>MDNA</i> debuted at number one in <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>, selling 32,000 copies in its first week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-can_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-can-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia, the album debuted at number one and was certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA) for shipments of 35,000 copies during its first week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ariacerti_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-ariacerti-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> It became Madonna's tenth chart-topping album in Australia, which made her the solo artist with the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association#Artists_with_the_most_number-one_albums" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">most number-one albums</a> of all time, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Barnes" title="Jimmy Barnes">Jimmy Barnes</a>, and pushed her behind only The Beatles with fourteen and <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> with eleven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> In Japan, <i>MDNA</i> debuted at number four on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> weekly albums chart with first week sales of 31,000 physical units. In the same week, her <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a>-released box set, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Complete_Studio_Albums_(1983_%E2%80%93_2008)" title="The Complete Studio Albums (1983 – 2008)">The Complete Studio Albums (1983 – 2008)</a></i>, also debuted at number nine, making Madonna the first international female artist in Japanese chart history to have two albums in the top ten simultaneously and the first international artist in 20 years to achieve such feat, since <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> in 1992. With those two releases, Madonna has accumulated 22 top-ten albums in Japan, more than any other international artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oricon_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-oricon-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_Japan" title="Recording Industry Association of Japan">Recording Industry Association of Japan</a> for shipments of 100,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaj_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaj-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> In India, the album shipped gold in its first week of release and became the country's fastest-selling international album of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-india_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-india-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna also set record for a foreign album in Turkey as <i>MDNA</i> sold over 30,000 copies within four days, outselling all Turkish domestic albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turkey_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-turkey-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, the album debuted at the top of the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> with first week sales of 56,335 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicweek_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-musicweek-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> It became Madonna's twelfth album to top the chart, breaking the record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> as the solo artist with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_artists_by_number_of_UK_Albums_Chart_number_ones" title="List of artists by number of UK Albums Chart number ones">most number-one albums</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicweek_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-musicweek-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Only <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> have more number-one albums in British chart history with fifteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicweek_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-musicweek-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The album slipped to number seven in its second week and number 13 in its third week, making it the first Madonna studio album not to be in the top ten on its third week on the chart since 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>MDNA</i> was certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI) for shipment of 100,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpi_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpi-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2012, the album had sold 112,765 copies in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uksales_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-uksales-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In Germany, the album was certified gold in its first week by the <a href="/wiki/Bundesverband_Musikindustrie" title="Bundesverband Musikindustrie">Bundesverband Musikindustrie</a> (BVMI) for shipments of 100,000 copies and debuted at number three on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_Control_Charts" title="Media Control Charts">Media Control</a> albums chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bvmi_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-bvmi-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-germany_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-germany-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> In Russia, album debuted atop the chart with 26,000 sold and was certified double platinum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-russia_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-russia-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> It became the best-selling album of 2012 in Russia with seven times platinum certification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-russia_year_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-russia_year-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a> (IFPI), <i>MDNA</i> was the twelfth global best-selling album of 2012 with sales of 1.8 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> To date, the album has sold about two million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwsales_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwsales-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvww_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvww-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<ul>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^a</a></b></span></sup> signifies a co-<a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>

<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_c"><b><a href="#ref_c">^c</a></b></span></sup> signifies a <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remixer</a> and additional <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formats">Formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=MDNA_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Digital Nightlife edition – <a href="/wiki/Smirnoff" title="Smirnoff">Smirnoff</a> announced an exclusive album through their <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> page. The album titled <i>MDNA Nightlife Edition</i> contains seven tracks from the album plus one exclusive remix of "Masterpiece", four remixes (one exclusive) of "Give Me All Your Luvin'" and two exclusive remixes of "Turn Up The Radio". Initially, the album was to be available worldwide but was then made exclusive to the United States, Smirnoff apologised that it was a technical error, thus making it available for download for $3.50 for a limited time only.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hipdigital1_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-hipdigital1-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facebook1_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-facebook1-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Digital Nightlife UK Remix EP – Smirnoff also released on April 13, 2012, a free remix EP through their UK Facebook page which includes three remixes of "Give Me All Your Luvin'", one of "Masterpiece" and three remixes of "Turn Up the Radio" (one of which is exclusive to the UK).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facebook2_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-facebook2-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Vinyl deluxe edition – 17 tracks; includes the deluxe version on two 12" vinyl discs to be released April 16, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
